Palmap has mapped out 15,000 high value locations and estimates the total market size for China is 100,000 locations.  Basically, Palmap has only mapped out 15% of the country. Palmap has changed its business model to become an LBS / indoor mapping data platform.  They are no longer an SI, but they will provide data and empower consumer apps, SIs, software firms and even the international big boys like Cisco.  Under the new business model, the more apps and SIs that use Palmap's data, the better.  It is a bet on the growth of the overall sector instead of on a single breakout consumer app.  I like the shift in strategy, but told them to figure out how to open the API and create a tool kit so that the location owners can automatically upload their indoor data onto Palmap's platform.  By opening the "supply" side, only then can Palmap create a true platform & ecosystem and the corresponding barriers to entry if Gaode or Baidu decide to jump into this space.  Zhang Yang will go back and think about this.******weizhibijiWiz|||wing@gobivc.com|||2013-10-14 00:00:00|||2013-10-20 00:00:00|||Communication re/ product plan, new version of Android APP and web version would launch by the end of October.******weizhibijiWiz|||wing@gobivc.com|||2013-10-21 00:00:00|||2013-10-27 00:00:00|||Writing 3Q2013 report.******weizhibijiWiz|||ken@gobivc.com|||2013-11-05 00:00:00|||2013-11-05 00:00:00|||Review in BJ ******weizhibijiWiz|||jason@gobivc.com|||2013-11-04 00:00:00|||2013-11-10 00:00:00|||review the product plan, arrange FA meeting and will join VC day.******weizhibijiWiz|||wing@gobivc.com|||2013-11-04 00:00:00|||2013-11-10 00:00:00|||2013 Jan~Oct review in BJ. Participants: Feargal Mooney (CEO), Catherine Gilvarry (Head of Marketing)

- Started in 1999, based in Dublin, Ireland
- 2013 had US$100 million revenues and US$30 million EBITDA; driven by ~40 million room-nights per year)
- 250 employees, mostly in Dublin; Shanghai office but really just for supply support for Greater Asia
- Now want to drive demand in Asia (currently mostly from Europe)

- Hostel defined as places with dormitory elements (i.e. shared room/bath)
- Sector has moved towards private independent hostels (as opposed to YMCAs)
- Hostel chains now getting backing from PE firms; Hostelworld is majority owned by Helmut Friedman (PE in San Francisco)
- Airbnb and Homeaway are not viewed as competitors, as they have different products, jurisdiction issues etc.
- Booking.com would be a competitor, as they are moving into hostels and vacation rentals

- 2003 acquired hostels.com, which was san francisco-based
- 2013 acquired hostelbookers.com, which was UK-based
- Now the group includes hostelworld.com/hostels.com (one backend platform), hostelbookers.com (different backend & database)
- One central supply chain team, but it deals with two backends

- Website booking: 12-15% deposit via website (which is also their commission), balance to hostel when they arrive
- Drive traffic through pay-per-click, SEO, brand awareness campaigns on social networks
- 70% of customers are 18-35 years old
- Hostelworld.com also has social element, with UGC, communities etc.******youduoduolvhangwang|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-04-14 00:00:00|||2014-04-20 00:00:00|||Follow-up w/ Hostelworld re: NDA signing - first 1.5 years doing reward moments in games, now doing fitness and others (2500 total app partnerships)
- case study: photo application (perfect365) for girls to try makeup 
  - several mn DAU (mostly in N. America), avg user uses 16min/day
  - wanted to: 1) monetize users without intrusive banner ads; happiness moments - one reward per user per day, a) upload photo, add filters, then click favorite for photos they like, b) share photo on social media. surprise & delight (random) rewards! (for camera360 perhaps reward for trying out new filters, downloading new effects, collage creation; find several moments to test) 
	       2) improve engagement & retention; kiip users come back 31% more often, 103% min longer per session
               3) find way to work w/ brand partners like MAC, Sephora, P&G, Unilever, J&J, McD's who want leverage user base

 - majority of Kiip's campaigns in US, but can cover up to 25 countries
 - team in colombia, UK, Japan to help work w/ brand agencies
 - about to work w/ McD's and Unilever in China (Bryan in Shanghai)

 - Kiip has SDK to help apps run their own campaigns using Kiip rewards technology

 - 50/50 revshare on every reward that is redeemed (for Kiip-sourced rewards)
 - $0.05 licensing fee on every reward that is redeemed (for App-sourced rewards)******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-04-07 00:00:00|||2014-04-13 00:00:00|||Liaise w/ Singtel organizers re: event details******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-04-14 00:00:00|||2014-04-20 00:00:00|||Attend Singtel CEO Forum w/ Cam360 management******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-04-14 00:00:00|||2014-04-20 00:00:00|||Attend Camera360 Board Meeting in Beijing******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-04-14 00:00:00|||2014-04-20 00:00:00|||Follow-up w/ Kiip: push forward NDA; SDK setup within Camera360; coordinate for test campaigns in Japan / Thailand******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-04-14 00:00:00|||2014-04-20 00:00:00|||Coordinate and arrange meetings for next week's trip to ASEAN******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-04-14 00:00:00|||2014-04-20 00:00:00|||Meeting w/ Hon Mun in Beijing re: trip to Thailand; ultimately decided to arrange meetings w/ AIS directly******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-04-14 00:00:00|||2014-04-20 00:00:00|||Call w/ Ben Yu from Sierra re: Camera360 in US; Ben will ask Facebook/Google corpdev to gauge interest for collaboraion******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-04-14 00:00:00|||2014-04-20 00:00:00|||Meeting w/ Camera360 management in Chengdu to streamline and prioritize overseas market strategy
- Markets to be divided into 3 development stages: 1) user acquisition, 2) basic monetization (in-app purchases), 3) advanced monetization (O2O, advertising)
- each development stage to be defined by market penetration/share (% of total smartphones) OR total MAU
- Stage 1 Markets: Japan, Indonesia, Korea, India, USA
- Stage 2 Markets: Singapore, Philippines, Vietnam
- Stage 3 Markets: China, Thailand, Malaysia
- Different stage markets to have different developmental priorities and different resource requirements******Camera360|||bruce@gobivc.com|||2014-04-14 00:00:00|||2014-04-20 00:00:00|||召开董事会，讨论产品方向和下一轮融资安排******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-04-21 00:00:00|||2014-04-27 00:00:00|||Trip to ASEAN: meetings w/ AIS, True, Globe, Smart, Telekom Malaysia, Digi, Maxis, Singtel, Starhub, aCommerce, Formation8******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-05-05 00:00:00|||2014-05-11 00:00:00|||Follow-up Singtel Collaboration for Co-Marketing Event on May 15-16******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-05-05 00:00:00|||2014-05-11 00:00:00|||Call w/ Airtel re: Camera360 in India

 - market environment is still good, but window is closing (prob soon after Jindong IPO and maybe even before Alibaba IPO)
 - user growth will continue to make up most of rationale for valuation; ideas for monetization and a few case studies would be icing on the cake

 - meitu valuation not sure or publicized; may pose challenge for camera360 valuation if user base is compared
 - if user growth rate peters out, or monetization seems too far, may also pose challenges for valuation (will have better idea once initial DD is conducted)

 - ekai believes company valuation could reach ~US$300 million if we can create competition amongst investors
 - suggests US$50-60m on US$300m would be reasonable in terms of investment amount (depends on existing investors' pro rata)

 - fees will be based on valuation (1% on US$200m -> 2% on US300m) 
 - SIG suggested to create incentive formula for amount raised over US$200m valuation
 - aim for max 15% total dilution in this round
 - we will say that we are planning to take pro rata, but depending on size of round and investor/mgmt team interest, we could consider options as well******Camera360|||tom@gobivc.com|||2014-05-20 00:00:00|||2014-05-20 00:00:00|||Thoughts from Richard Chang after his visit to Chengdu in April.  He thinks Camera360 has a better shot at being a "tools" company and being acquired than becoming a "total solutions" company.  Camera360 may need to develop a social network, but creating an SNS now is very difficult.   Qualcomm succeeded by going to Korea with its chips; perhaps Camera360 should look outside of China.  Camera360 should consider partnering with Ofoto, SmugMug, SnapFish - firms with established networks that are hard to displace.  We should also determine who needs a photo app i.e. Skype, Viber, and Tango.  Richard feels that Camera360's positioning is not clear and confusing i.e. Why is video a separate product?  Why not just a feature?  Camera360 needs to religiously track user growth - DAU, MAU - upward trend has to point up.  As with all user dependent start-ups, if growth momentum stalls, Gobi needs to think about selling out in the Series C.  We also need to track user comments - lots of negative feedback on the blogs with complaints that Camera360 is confusing, complicated and not user friendly.  (Note: These comments were before the new verison was released.)  Richard also suggested that we need to build out an IP portfolio as that could be valuable and ultimately what an acquiror is paying for.  Richard has some contacts in Korea and suggested we approach Samsung and Naver.******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-05-26 00:00:00|||2014-06-01 00:00:00|||Set up follow-up meetings w/ Smart and Globe******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-05-26 00:00:00|||2014-06-01 00:00:00|||Coordinate follow-up items for Singtel cooperation******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-05-26 00:00:00|||2014-06-01 00:00:00|||Temporarily close loop on discussions w/ Kiip******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-05-26 00:00:00|||2014-06-01 00:00:00|||Liaise w/ Oka-san on potential collaboration w/ Docomo and FET******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-05-26 00:00:00|||2014-06-01 00:00:00|||Continue partnership discussions w/ aCommerce re: Huawei and Xiaomi******Camera360|||bruce@gobivc.com|||2014-06-16 00:00:00|||2014-06-22 00:00:00|||沟通联合投资硬件项目******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-06-23 00:00:00|||2014-06-29 00:00:00|||Calls w/ Globe, Smart, Singtel, AIS******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-07-02 00:00:00|||2014-07-05 00:00:00|||Call w/ Smart; to follow-up w/ Globe******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-07-03 00:00:00|||2014-07-06 00:00:00|||Initiate Rakuten/Viber discussion******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-07-07 00:00:00|||2014-07-13 00:00:00|||Review Smart/Globe partnership agreements******Camera360|||chibo@gobivc.com|||2014-07-07 00:00:00|||2014-07-13 00:00:00|||Update Kiip relationship (Brian Wong to visit Shanghai in July 21-22)******Camera360|||bruce@gobivc.com|||2014-08-04 00:00:00|||2014-08-10 00:00:00|||撰写年报******Camera360|||bruce@gobivc.com|||2014-08-18 00:00:00|||2014-08-24 00:00:00|||沟通成立成都WFOE一事******Camera360|||bruce@gobivc.com|||2014-08-18 00:00:00|||2014-08-24 00:00:00|||沟通成立成都WFOE一事******Camera360|||tom@gobivc.com|||2014-09-05 00:00:00|||2014-09-05 00:00:00|||Jason Wang learned that Meitu raised US$100 million from Tiger and Ceyuan on a pre-money valuation ofUS$600 million.
